Ideally, the plots in Figures A.1c and A.2c should show ﬂat lines, as this would mean that
the microphone vibrates exactly as the moving mass of the shaker and in-phase. The
15.0 cm rod shows an amplitude peak at Ω≈9 kHz both at the microphone and shaker
base level, which is probably caused by an axial eigenfrequency. The 7.5 cm conical rod
behaves unexpectedly, as it yields a large amplitude for the shaker level at Ω> 8 kHz,
which is only partially visible in the microphone amplitude curve. The axial vibration
amplitude of the microphone housing decreases when mounted on conical rods, hinting
that the weight has an impact on the axial amplitude.
All the rod designs have been weighted:

35.43 g,

13.46 g ,
and the moving mass of the shaker is 18 g.

A.4
Assumption of Incident Wave Pressure
The following test is performed to validate the assumption from Section 4.1.5, that an
incident sound pressure wave will propagate as a uniformly distributed force on the
diaphragm. The ﬁndings turned out to be of little interest to the thesis, which is why
they are found here.
In this test, only the air is modeled while all structural geometry remains unmeshed,
hence creating a contour of the microphone in the air mesh. The mesh and the solved
model are shown in Figure A.9:
90
==PAGE:106==
Appendix A. Supplementary Analyses
(A) Air mesh and pressure wave.
(B) Pressure distribution.
FIGURE A.9: Pressure distribution test in ANSYS.
Though the contour plot in Figure A.9b seems to show no pressure difference along
the membrane line, some selected nodal pressure solutions are recorded and plotted
in Figure A.10 for a better resolution of the local domain. Different conﬁgurations are
tested, Figure A.10a is the standard conﬁguration, showing results obtained with the
mesh and pressure wave shown in Figure A.9a, Lp = 20 dB SPL, and Ωmax = 100 Hz
almost resembling the static solution. The pressure along the different nodes are fairly
constant. Figure A.10c, is solved for Lp = 100 dB SPL, Ωmax = 20 kHz, and a much ﬁner
mesh. Although starting at the same spot, the pressure along the membrane is proven
to increase when getting closer to the edge as a function of higher frequencies. The
model is also solved for the same parameters but with Lp = 20 dB SPL, yielding the
same results except for a different pressure amplitude (not shown). So a ﬁner mesh and
a larger sound pressure does not seem to affect the membrane pressure distribution, but
frequency does. Applying the pressure in only a single node rather than a line of nodes
(Figure A.10b) affect not only the magnitude, but also the pressure distribution, where
the center point on the membrane experiences a slightly larger pressure than the edge.
91
==PAGE:107==
Appendix A. Supplementary Analyses

)^2*omega_nj(1,j)*((Omega_rad)^2−(omega_nj(1,j))^2));
213
end
214
w(i) = abs(2*sqrt(2)*F0/(rho*t_mem*R)*w1);
215
end
216
% Calculating the static solution analytically.
217
w_ana=F0*R^2/(N*4);
218

APPENDIX
E
SCRIPTS FOR NUMERICAL ANALYSES
This appendix provides the ANSYS scripts used to perform the numerical analyses in
Chapters 2 and 4. No style package for listing the APDL-language in LATEX is readily
available, as is the case for the Matlab-language, so in order to display it in a properly
color formatted and easily readable manner, the authors wrote the styling themselves.
E.1
Scripts for Membrane Analyses
E.1.1
Script for the Rectangular Membrane
Tree diagram of the ANSYS script:
Membrane_Rectangular.txt
Build the geometry.
Select solution type: Static, modal, or harmonic.
If harmonic: Set the sampling frequency spectrum.
Set the mesh refinement.
Apply pre-tension to the membrane.
Solve.
Post-process the results.
1
FINISH
2
/CLEAR
3
4
/TITLE,'Rectangular membrane'
5
/FILNAME,'Mem_rec'
! Set file name for outputs.

Appendix E. APDL Code
6
7
! This script assumes that the user has the Macros included in the thesis appendix either in the ANSYS
working folder or the folder specified below.
8
/PSEARCH,'.\Dropbox\Delemapper\Nikolaj & Johan\ANSYS\Macros\'
9
/PREP7
10
11
/NERR,,,,,0
! The number of invalid command warnings before a stop warning will be issued:
0 Disables the stop warning/error function.
12
/UIS,MSGPOP,3
! Controls which messages from the ANSYS error message subroutine are
displayed in a message dialog box: 3 Only errors displayed.
13
*AFUN,DEG
! Use degrees, [deg], as the angular unit.
14
15
! Membrane material constants
16
E_mem=5e9
! [Pa], E−modulus.
17
nu_mem=0.4
! [−], Poisson's ratio.
18
rho_mem=1400
! [kg/m^3], Density.
19
t_mem=1.5e−6
! [m], Membrane thickness.
20
a_length=0.00195
! [m], Side length a.
21
b_length=0.00295
! [m], Side length b.
22
P=5.2/t_mem
! [Pa], Membrane pretension.
23
alpha_mem=117e−6
! [m/(m*Celcius)], Coefficient of thermal expansion (arbitrary).
24
T=−P/(E_mem/(1−nu_mem)*alpha_mem) ! [Celcius], Calculated temperature to give pre−tension.
25
26
F0=0.5
! [N/m^2], Force applied to membrane (not needed for modes).
27
28
debug=0
! Set to 1 if you do not want ANSYS to prompt your inputs. 0 if you do.

*IF,debug,EQ,0,THEN

*ASK,soltype,'Select solution type: Simple=>1, Modal=>2, Harmonic=>3',1
31
*IF,soltype,EQ,3,THEN
32
multi_freq_rectangular
33
*ENDIF
34
*ASK,N,'Select mesh refinement:',20 ![−], Mesh refinement, 10 is relatively coarse and 30 is fine.
35
*ELSE
36
! Parameters used when debug=1
37
soltype=1
! Set to 1 just for simple solution and view pre−stress, 2 for modal analysis,
and 3 for harmonic analysis.
38
f_start=0
! [Hz], Sweeping start.
39
f_end=50000
! [Hz], Sweeping end.
40
f_incr=100
! [Hz], Sweep increment size.
41
N=20
! [−], Mesh refinement, 10 is coarse number. 30 is fine.
42
*ENDIF

sweep.

Appendix E. APDL Code
E.2.3
Script of the Numerical Modeling of the Square Sonion 50GC31 Mi-
crophone (3D)
Tree diagram of the ANSYS script:
Microphone_Rectangular_3D.txt
Select mirrorsymmetry or full model.
Build the geometry.
Select how to mount the microphone on the rod.
Model air or no air.
Mesh geometry.
Apply pre-tension to the membrane.
Excite the microphone by user-input or experiment input.
If user-input excitation: Set the sampling frequency spectrum.
If experiment input excitation: Set the number of steps to run.
Solve.
Post-process the results.
1
FINISH
2
/CLEAR

/TITLE,'Rectangular microphone, 3D'
